**Judah and Israel**  - The people of Judah and Israel were all descendants of Jacob and part of God's people. Even so, they disobeyed God and fought and killed each other.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__18-09|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/18-the-divided-kingdom|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__18-11|>>]]**


===== The Evil Kings of Israel [18-11] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-18-11.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=51c4a9?nolink&640x360}}


In the new **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom|kingdom]]** of **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/israel|Israel]]**, all the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/king|kings]]** were **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/evil|evil]]**. Many of these kings were killed by other **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/israel|Israelites]]** who wanted to become king in their place.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**Israelites**  - Here, “Israelites” refers only to the people living in the northern kingdom of Israel, not to the people living in the southern kingdom of Judah.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__18-10|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/18-the-divided-kingdom|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__18-12|>>]]**


===== Israel Worshiped Idols [18-12] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-18-12.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=567333?nolink&640x360}}


All of the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/king|kings]]** and most of the people of the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom-of-israel|kingdom of Israel]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/worship|worshiped]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/idol|idols]]**. Their idol worship often included sexual immorality and sometimes even **child [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/sacrifice|sacrifice]]**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**child sacrifice**  - They killed children as offerings to some of their idols.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__18-11|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/18-the-divided-kingdom|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__18-13|>>]]**


===== Judah Was Unfaithful [18-13] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-18-13.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=07ea16?nolink&640x360}}


The **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/king|kings]]** of **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom-of-judah|Judah]]** were **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/descendant|descendants]]** of **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/david|David]]**. Some of these kings were **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/good|good]]** men who **ruled [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/justice|justly]]** and **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/worship|worshiped]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]**. But most of Judah’s kings were **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/evil|evil]]**, **corrupt**, and they worshiped **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/idol|idols]]**. Some of the kings even **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/sacrifice|sacrificed]]** their children to false **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god-false|gods]]**. Most of the people of Judah also **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/rebel|rebelled]]** against God and worshiped other gods.


//A Bible story from: 1 Kings 1-6; 11-12//


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**ruled justly**  - This means they ruled according to God's laws. This can be translated as, “when they ruled, they did what was right.”
    * 


**corrupt**  - This can be translated as, “did what was wrong in order to get whatever they wanted.”
    * 


//A Bible story from//  - These references may be slightly different in some Bible translations.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__18-12|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/18-the-divided-kingdom|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-01|>>]]**


===== God Sent the Prophets [19-01] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-19-01.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=58d1c0?nolink&640x360}}


**Throughout the history of**  the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/israel|Israelites]]**, **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** sent them **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophets]]**. The prophets heard messages from God and then told the people God’s messages.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**Throughout the history of**  - This expression means that God sent many prophets at many different times during all of the years that Israel and Judah existed.
    * 


**Israelites**  - This could be translated here as, “the kingdoms of Israel and Judah.” All of the descendants of Jacob, including those in the kingdom of Judah, continued to be called “Israelites.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__18-13|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/19-the-prophets|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-02|>>]]**


===== Elijah Rebuked Ahab [19-02] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-19-02.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=65ffde?nolink&640x360}}


**[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/elijah|Elijah]]** was a **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophet]]** when **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/ahab|Ahab]]** was **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/king|king]]** over the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom-of-israel|kingdom of Israel]]**. Ahab was an **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/evil|evil]]** man who encouraged people to **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/worship|worship]]** a false **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god-false|god]]** named **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/baal|Baal]]**. Elijah said to Ahab, “There will be no rain or dew in the kingdom of Israel **until I say so**.” **This made Ahab very angry**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**until I say so**  - This may be translated as, “until I command the rain and dew to come again.”
    * 


**This made Ahab very angry**  – This could be translated as, “When Ahab heard what Elijah said, he became very angry.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-01|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/19-the-prophets|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-03|>>]]**


===== God Provided for Elijah [19-03] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-19-03.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=eb8dac?nolink&640x360}}


**[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** told **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/elijah|Elijah]]** to go to a stream in **the wilderness**  to hide from Ahab who wanted to kill him. Every morning and every evening, birds would bring him bread and meat. **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/ahab|Ahab]]** and his army looked for Elijah, but they could not find him. **The drought**  was so severe that the stream eventually dried up.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**the wilderness**  - This was a remote location with very few people. This may also be translated as, “desert” or, “the bush.”
    * 


**The drought**  - This could be translated as, “the lack of rain.” This drought was a result of Elijah declaring that there would be no rain.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-02|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/19-the-prophets|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-04|>>]]**


===== God Provided for the Widow [19-04] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-19-04.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=396aa1?nolink&640x360}}


So **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/elijah|Elijah]]** went to a **neighboring country**. A widow and her son in that country had almost run out of food because of **the famine**. But they **took care of**  Elijah, and **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]] provided for them so that their flour jar and their bottle of oil never became empty**. They had food through the whole famine. Elijah stayed there for several years.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**neighboring country**  - This refers to a country that was beside, or shared a border with Israel.
    * 


**the famine**  - If needed, this could be translated as, “the famine caused by the drought.”
    * 


**took care of**  – This means they gave him a place to stay in their house and provided food for him. It does not mean he was sick.
    * 


**God provided for them…never became empty**  - This could be translated as, “God prevented their flour jar and their bottle of oil from becoming empty” or, “God caused…to never become empty.”
    * 


**flour jar**  - This refers to a clay jar in which the widow kept her supply of flour.
    * 


**bottle of oil**  - In Israel, olive oil is used for cooking. This could be translated as, “bottle of cooking oil.” The widow used the flour and the oil for making bread.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-03|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/19-the-prophets|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-05|>>]]**


===== Elijah Challenged Ahab [19-05] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-19-05.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=2714b7?nolink&640x360}}


After three and a half years, **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** told **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/elijah|Elijah]]** to return to the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom-of-israel|kingdom of Israel]]** and **speak with [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/ahab|Ahab]] because he was going to send**rain again. When Ahab saw Elijah he said, “There you are, **you troublemaker**!” Elijah replied to him, “You are the troublemaker! **You have abandoned [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/yahweh|Yahweh]]**, the true God, and **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/worship|worshiped]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/baal|Baal]]**. Bring all the people of the kingdom of Israel to **Mount Carmel**.”


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**speak with Ahab because he was going to send**  – This could be translated as, “tell Ahab that God was going to send.”
    * 


**you troublemaker**  - This means, “You are a troublemaker!” Ahab was accusing Elijah of causing trouble by telling the king that he was doing wrong and also by stopping the rain.
    * 


**You have abandoned Yahweh**  - That is, Ahab had led Israel to stop worshiping and obeying Yahweh.
    * 


**Mount Carmel**  - Mount Carmel is the name of a mountain located in northern Israel. It is over 500 meters high.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-04|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/19-the-prophets|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-06|>>]]**


===== Elijah and the Prophets of Baal [19-06] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-19-06.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=ed1ac2?nolink&640x360}}


All the people of the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom-of-israel|kingdom of Israel]]**, including the 450 **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophets]]** of **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/baal|Baal]]**, came to **Mount Carmel**. **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/elijah|Elijah]]** said to the people, “**How long will you**  keep changing your mind? **If [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/yahweh|Yahweh]] is [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]**, serve him! **If Baal is God**, serve him!”


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**Mount Carmel**  - See how you translated this in **[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-05|[19-05]]]**.
    * 


**How long will you**  - This is not a real question asking for information. Elijah was rebuking the Israelites for repeatedly changing their minds about whether they would serve Yahweh or Baal. Some languages will have to express this as a statement such as, “Stop changing your minds about whom you will worship!”
    * 


**If Yahweh is God…If Baal is God**  - This does not mean that Elijah was undecided. He knew that Yahweh is the real God. He wanted the people to understand that when they worship false gods, they are rejecting Yahweh as the only true God. Translate this in a way that shows that the people had to make a choice.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-05|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/19-the-prophets|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-07|>>]]**


===== A Sacrifice without Fire [19-07] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-19-07.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=b34d63?nolink&640x360}}


Then **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/elijah|Elijah]]** said to the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophets]]** of **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/baal|Baal]]**, “Kill a bull and prepare it as a **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/sacrifice|sacrifice]]**, but do not light the fire. I will do the same. The **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]] who answers with fire**is **the real God**.” So the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/priest|priests]]** of Baal prepared a sacrifice but did not light the fire.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**who answers with fire**  - That is, “who supernaturally sends fire to burn up the sacrifice.”
    * 


**the real God**  - This means the one and only true God.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-06|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/19-the-prophets|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-08|>>]]**


===== Baal Did Not Answer [19-08] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-19-08.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=84d6bd?nolink&640x360}}


Then the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophets]]** of **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/baal|Baal]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/pray|prayed]] to Baal**, “Hear us, Baal!” All day long they prayed and **shouted**  and even **cut themselves with knives**, but **there was no answer**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**prayed to Baal**  - the prophets of Baal asked Baal to send fire onto the bull they prepared as a sacrifice.
    * 


**shouted**  - They yelled or called out loudly to Baal.
    * 


**cut themselves with knives**  - They injured themselves with knives as an extreme way to show their devotion to Baal, hoping that this would persuade him to listen to them.
    * 


**there was no answer**  - There was no response of any kind to their shouting, and no fire came to burn up the sacrifice.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-07|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/19-the-prophets|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-09|>>]]**


===== Elijah Prepared the Sacrifice [19-09] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-19-09.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=df3175?nolink&640x360}}


At the end of the day, **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/elijah|Elijah]]** prepared a **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/sacrifice|sacrifice]]** to **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]**. Then he told the people to pour twelve huge pots of water on top of the sacrifice until the meat, the wood, and even the ground around the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/altar|altar]]** were completely wet.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


//(There are no notes for this frame.)// 
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-08|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/19-the-prophets|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-10|>>]]**


===== The Prayer of Elijah [19-10] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-19-10.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=2978f0?nolink&640x360}}


Then **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/elijah|Elijah]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/pray|prayed]]**, “**[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/yahweh|Yahweh]]**, **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** of **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/abraham|Abraham]]**, **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/isaac|Isaac]]**, and **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/jacob|Jacob]]**, **show us**  today that you are the God of **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/israel|Israel]]** and that **I am your [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/servant|servant]]**. **Answer me**  so that **these people will know**  that you are the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/true|true]]** God.”


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**show us**  - That is, “prove to us” or, “demonstrate to us.”
    * 


**I am your servant**  - This could be translated as, “You have given me authority to serve you and do these things.”
    * 


**Answer me**  - That is, “respond to my prayer” or, “send the fire that I have asked you for.”
    * 


**these people will know**  - This may be translated as, “these people will see and understand.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-09|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/19-the-prophets|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-11|>>]]**


===== God Answered with Fire [19-11] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-19-11.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=52ce63?nolink&640x360}}


Immediately, fire **fell from the sky**  and burned up the meat, the wood, the rocks, the dirt, and even the water that was around the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/altar|altar]]**. When the people saw this, they **fell on the ground**  and said, “**[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/yahweh|Yahweh]] is [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]**! Yahweh is God!”


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**fell from the sky**  - This may be translated as, “suddenly came down from the sky.”
    * 


**fell on the ground**  - They quickly lay down or knelt down on the ground. They were afraid of Yahweh because they had seen his power. They knew that only the true God could do that and bowed down to honor and worship him.
    * 


**Yahweh is God**  - This expression means that they understood that Yahweh is the only God, not just one god among others.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-10|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/19-the-prophets|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-12|>>]]**


===== Killing the Prophets of Baal [19-12] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-19-12.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=e97708?nolink&640x360}}


Then **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/elijah|Elijah]]** said, “Do not let any of the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophets]]** of **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/baal|Baal]] escape**!” So the people **captured**  the prophets of Baal. Then Elijah took them away from there and killed them.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**escape**  - The prophets of Baal tried to run away after their god was proven to be a false god.
    * 


**captured**  – That is, “seized and held onto” or, “took hold of.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-11|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/19-the-prophets|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-13|>>]]**


===== A Storm Ended the Drought [19-13] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-19-13.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=2b01c5?nolink&640x360}}


Then **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/elijah|Elijah]]** said to **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/king|King]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/ahab|Ahab]]**, “Return immediately to the city, because the rain is coming.” Soon **the sky grew black**, and a heavy rain began. **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/yahweh|Yahweh]]** had ended the **drought**  and proved that he is the true **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**the sky grew black**  - That is, “the sky became very dark.” Heavy rainclouds covered the sky, making it look dark grey or black.
    * 


**drought**  – That is, “long dry time with no rain.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-12|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/19-the-prophets|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-14|>>]]**


===== Naaman Came to Elisha [19-14] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-19-14.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=7b4f8d?nolink&640x360}}


After the time of **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/elijah|Elijah]]**, **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** chose a man named Elisha to be his **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophet]]**. God did many **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/miracle|miracles]]** through Elisha. One of the miracles happened to **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/naaman|Naaman]]**, **an enemy commander**, who had a horrible skin disease. **He had heard of Elisha**  so **he went and asked Elisha**  to **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/heal|heal]]** him. Elisha told Naaman to dip himself seven times in the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/jordan-river|Jordan River]]**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**an enemy commander**  - Naaman was a commander in the army of one of the countries that was Israel's enemy.
    * 


**He had heard of Elisha**  - This means that people had told Naaman that Elisha was able to perform miracles.
    * 


**he went and asked Elisha**  - That is, “he went to see Elisha and asked him.” Naaman had to go into Israel to find Elisha and ask him to do this.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-13|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/19-the-prophets|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-15|>>]]**


===== Naaman Was Healed [19-15] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-19-15.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=48eff8?nolink&640x360}}


At first **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/naaman|Naaman]]** was angry and **would not do it because it seemed foolish**. But later **he changed his mind**  and dipped himself seven times in the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/jordan-river|Jordan River]]**. When he came up the last time, his skin was completely **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/heal|healed]]**! **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** had healed him.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**would not do it because it seemed foolish**  - Naaman would not do what Elisha said because he knew that washing alone could not heal his disease.
    * 


**he changed his mind**  - That is, “he decided to do what Elisha had told him to do.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-14|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/19-the-prophets|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-16|>>]]**


===== The Prophets Warned the People [19-16] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-19-16.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=097c86?nolink&640x360}}


**[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** sent many other **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophets]]**. They all told the people to stop **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/worship|worshiping]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/idol|idols]]** and to **start showing [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/justice|justice]] and [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/mercy|mercy]]** to others. The prophets warned the people that if they did not stop doing **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/evil|evil]]** and start **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/obey|obeying]]** God, then God would **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/judge|judge]]** them as **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/guilt|guilty]]**, and he would **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/punish|punish]]** them.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**start showing justice and mercy**  - This can be translated as, “start being just and merciful” or, “begin to demonstrate justice and mercy.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-15|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/19-the-prophets|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-17|>>]]**


===== Jeremiah Suffered for God [19-17] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-19-17.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=9bff7d?nolink&640x360}}


Most of the time, the people did not **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/obey|obey]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]**. They often mistreated the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophets]]** and sometimes even killed them. Once, the prophet **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/jeremiah|Jeremiah]]** was put into a **dry well**  and left there to die. He sank down into the mud that was in the bottom of the well, but then the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/king|king]] had [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/mercy|mercy]] on him**and ordered his servants to pull Jeremiah out of the well before he died.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**dry well**  - The well did not currently have any water in it, but it did still have mud in the bottom. This could be translated as, “empty well.”
    * 


**had mercy on him**  – This means he was kind to Jeremiah and helped him.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-16|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/19-the-prophets|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-18|>>]]**


===== The Message of the Prophets [19-18] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-19-18.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=be0e12?nolink&640x360}}


The **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophets]] continued to speak for [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** even though the people hated them. They warned people that God would destroy them if they did not **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/repent|repent]]**. They also reminded people **of the [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/promise|promise]] that God’s [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/messiah|Messiah]] would come**.


//A Bible story from: 1 Kings 16-18; 2 Kings 5; Jeremiah 38//


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**continued to speak for God**  - That is, “continued to tell the people what God wanted to tell them.”
    * 


**of the promise that God's Messiah would come**  – This could be translated as, “that God had promised that his Messiah would come to save his people.”
    * 


//A Bible story from//  - These references may be slightly different in some Bible translations.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-17|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/19-the-prophets|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-01|>>]]**


===== Israel Sinned [20-01] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-20-01.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=395aa1?nolink&640x360}}


The **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom-of-israel|kingdom of Israel]]** and the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom-of-judah|kingdom of Judah]]** both **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/sin|sinned]]** against **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]**. They **broke the [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/covenant|covenant]]** that God had made with them at **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/sinai|Sinai]]**. God sent his **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophets]]** to **warn them to [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/repent|repent]]** and **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/worship|worship]]** him again, but they refused to **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/obey|obey]]**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**broke the covenant**  - That is, “disobeyed the commands God had given them in his covenant with them at Mount Sinai.”
    * 


**warn them to repent and worship him again**  – Another way to translate this would be, “tell them to stop sinning and to worship Yahweh instead of other gods, or terrible things would happen to them.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__19-18|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/20-the-exile-and-return|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-02|>>]]**


===== Assyria Destroyed Israel [20-02] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-20-02.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=9cec18?nolink&640x360}}


So **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/punish|punished]] both kingdoms**by allowing their enemies to destroy them. The **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/assyria|Assyrian Empire]]**, a powerful, cruel nation, destroyed the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom-of-israel|kingdom of Israel]]**. The Assyrians killed many people in the kingdom of Israel, **took away**  everything of value, and burned much of the country.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**both kingdoms**  - This refers to both the kingdoms of Israel and Judah.
    * 


**Empire**  - A country was called an “empire” when it was powerful enough to extend its authority over many other countries.
    * 


**took away**  - That is, “stole.” They stole these valuable things and carried them back to Assyria.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-01|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/20-the-exile-and-return|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-03|>>]]**


===== Israel Was Removed from the Land [20-03] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-20-03.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=2d75dc?nolink&640x360}}


The **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/assyria|Assyrians]]** gathered all the leaders, the rich people, and the people with **skills**  and took them to Assyria. Only the very poor **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/israel|Israelites]]** who had not been killed **remained**  in the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom-of-israel|kingdom of Israel]]**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**skills**  – This refers to practical skills such as woodworking, metalworking, and building.
    * 


**remained**  - That is, “stayed” or, “were left behind” or, “were allowed to stay behind.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-02|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/20-the-exile-and-return|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-04|>>]]**


===== Foreigners Were Brought to Israel [20-04] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-20-04.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=636408?nolink&640x360}}


Then the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/assyria|Assyrians]]** brought **foreigners**  to live in the land where the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom-of-israel|kingdom of Israel]]** had been. The foreigners rebuilt the destroyed cities and married the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/israel|Israelites]]** who were left there. The **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/descendant|descendants]]** of the Israelites who married foreigners were called **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/samaria|Samaritans]]**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**foreigners**  - This refers to people who were not Israelites.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-03|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/20-the-exile-and-return|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-05|>>]]**


===== Judah also Worshiped Idols [20-05] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-20-05.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=4ca569?nolink&640x360}}


The people in the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom-of-judah|kingdom of Judah]]** saw how **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** had **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/punish|punished]]** the people of the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom-of-israel|kingdom of Israel]]****for not [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/believe|believing]] and [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/obey|obeying]] him**. But they still **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/worship|worshiped]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/idol|idols]]**, including the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god-false|gods]]** of the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/canaan|Canaanites]]**. God sent **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophets]]** to **warn them**, but **they refused to listen**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**for not believing and obeying him**  – Another way to translate this would be, “because they did not believe or obey him.”
    * 


**warn them**  – That is, “tell them to stop sinning or terrible things would happen to them.”
    * 


**they refused to listen**  - That is, “they refused to obey” or “they refused to stop their evil behavior.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-04|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/20-the-exile-and-return|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-06|>>]]**


===== Judah Served Babylon [20-06] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-20-06.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=8e885a?nolink&640x360}}


About 100 years after the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/assyria|Assyrians]]** destroyed the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom-of-israel|kingdom of Israel]]**, **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** sent **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/nebuchadnezzar|Nebuchadnezzar]]**, **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/king|king]]** of the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/babylon|Babylonians]]**, to attack the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom-of-judah|kingdom of Judah]]**. **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/babylon|Babylon]]** was a powerful **empire**. The king of Judah agreed **to be Nebuchadnezzar’s [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/servant|servant]]** and pay him a lot of money every year.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**empire**  - See how you translated this in **[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-02|[20-02]]]**.
    * 


**agreed to be**  – The king of Judah was forced to either serve the Babylonian king or be destroyed.
    * 


**to be Nebuchadnezzar's servant**  - This could be translated as, “to govern Judah under Nebuchadnezzar's command.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-05|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/20-the-exile-and-return|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-07|>>]]**


===== Babylon Destroyed Judah [20-07] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-20-07.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=39af98?nolink&640x360}}


But after a few years, the king of **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom-of-judah|Judah]] [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/rebel|rebelled]]** against **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/babylon|Babylon]]**. So, the Babylonians **came back**  and attacked the kingdom of Judah. They **captured the city**  of **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/jerusalem|Jerusalem]]**, destroyed the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/temple|Temple]]**, and **took away**  all the treasures of the city and the Temple.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**came back**  - This may also be translated as, “returned” or “came to Judah again.”
    * 


**captured the city**  - That is, “took control of the city and the people there.”
    * 


**took away**  - They carried the treasures with them back to Babylon.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-06|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/20-the-exile-and-return|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-08|>>]]**


===== The Kind of Judah Was Punished [20-08] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-20-08.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=951f31?nolink&640x360}}


**To [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/punish|punish]]** the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/king|king]]** of **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom-of-judah|Judah]]** for rebelling, **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/nebuchadnezzar|Nebuchadnezzar's]]** soldiers killed the king’s **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/son|sons]] in front of him**and then **made him blind**. After that, they took the king away to die in prison in **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/babylon|Babylon]]**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**To punish**  - Nebuchadnezzar punished the king of Judah by telling his soldiers to do these things.
    * 


**in front of him**  - This may be translated as, “where he could see,” or “so that he could see it,” or “before his eyes.”
    * 


**made him blind**  - This may also be translated as, “destroyed his eyes.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-07|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/20-the-exile-and-return|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-09|>>]]**


===== Judah Was Taken to Babylon [20-09] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-20-09.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=5f333b?nolink&640x360}}


**[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/nebuchadnezzar|Nebuchadnezzar]]** and his army took almost all of the people of the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom-of-judah|kingdom of Judah]]** to **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/babylon|Babylon]]**, **leaving only the poorest people behind**  to plant the fields. **This period of time**  when **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God's]]** people were forced to leave the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/promised-land|Promised Land]]** is called the **Exile**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**leaving…behind**  - That is, “leaving only the poorest people in Judah” or, “letting only the poorest people stay in Judah.”
    * 


**This period of time**  - To translate this, choose a phrase that can refer to a long time, since this exile period lasted seventy years.
    * 


**Exile**  - The word “exile” means someone is removed from they country by force. The “Exile” is the term for this 70-year period when the Israelites were forced to live in Babylon.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-08|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/20-the-exile-and-return|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-10|>>]]**


===== God Remembered His Promise [20-10] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-20-10.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=bb0f22?nolink&640x360}}


Even though **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/punish|punished]]** his people for their **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/sin|sin]]** by taking them away into **exile**, he **did not forget**  them or his **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/promise|promises]]**. God continued to **watch over**  his people and **speak to them through his [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophets]]**. He promised that, after seventy years, they would return to the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/promised-land|Promised Land]]** again.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**exile**  - See how you translated this term in **[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-09|[20-09]]]**.
    * 


**did not forget**  - This could be translated as, “did not ignore” or, “did not neglect.” Or the whole phrase could be translated as, “continued to honor his commitment to his people and his promises.”
    * 


**watch over**  - That is, “take care of.”
    * 


**speak to them through his prophets**  - This could be translated as, “tell his prophets messages that he wanted them to tell his people.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-09|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/20-the-exile-and-return|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-11|>>]]**


===== Persia Defeated Babylon [20-11] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-20-11.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=21ea2f?nolink&640x360}}


About **seventy years later**, **Cyrus**, the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/king|king]]** of the **Persians**, defeated **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/babylon|Babylon]]**, so the Persian Empire replaced the Babylonian Empire. **The [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/israel|Israelites]] were now called [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/jew|Jews]]** and most of them had lived their whole lives in Babylon. Only a few very old Jews even remembered **the land of Judah**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**seventy years later**  - This refers to the seventy years that had passed since the Babylonian army took the people of Jerusalem into exile.
    * 


**Cyrus**  - Cyrus was also called, “Cyrus the Great.” The name “Cyrus” meant “like the sun” in the Persian language. However, since Cyrus was an important historical person, it might be best to transliterate his name, rather than translating the meaning.
    * 


**Persians**  - The Persian Empire grew to cover the area from central Asia to Egypt. Its home was located in the general area of modern-day Iran.
    * 


**The Israelites were now called Jews**  - This could also be translated as, “People now called the Israelites by the name 'Jews.'”
    * 


**the land of Judah**  - That is, the area where the kingdom of Judah was located before the Exile. Jerusalem was the capital city of Judah.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-10|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/20-the-exile-and-return|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-12|>>]]**


===== Cyrus Sent Judah Home [20-12] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-20-12.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=481d64?nolink&640x360}}


The **Persian Empire**  was strong but **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/mercy|merciful]]** to the people it conquered. Shortly after **Cyrus**  became king of the Persians, he gave an order that any **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/jew|Jew]]** who wanted **to return to Judah**  could leave Persia and go back to Judah. He even gave them money to rebuild the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/temple|Temple]]**! So, after seventy years in **exile**, a small group of Jews **returned**  to the city of **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/jerusalem|Jerusalem]]** in Judah.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**Persian Empire**  - See how you translated this term in **[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-11|[20-11]]]**.
    * 


**Cyrus**  - See how you translated his name in **[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-11|[20-11]]]**.
    * 


**Judah**  - See the note about Judah in **[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-11|[20-11]]]**.
    * 


**to return to Judah**  - Since most of these Jews were the children and grandchildren of those who left Judah, they had never lived in Judah before. In some languages it might be better to say “to go to Judah.”
    * 


**exile**  - See how you translated this term in **[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-09|[20-09]]]**.
    * 


**returned**  – That is, “went back.” Some languages may prefer to say, “went” since most of these people had never been to Jerusalem.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-11|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/20-the-exile-and-return|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-13|>>]]**


===== The Temple Was Rebuilt [20-13] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-20-13.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=056577?nolink&640x360}}


When **the people**  arrived in **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/jerusalem|Jerusalem]]**, they rebuilt the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/temple|Temple]]** and **the wall**  around the city. Although they were still **ruled by other people**, **once again**  they lived in the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/promised-land|Promised Land]]** and **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/worship|worshiped]] at the Temple**.


//A Bible story from: 2 Kings 17; 24-25; 2 Chronicles 36; Ezra 1-10; Nehemiah 1-13//


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**the people**  - That is, the Israelites, the descendants of Jacob, who were now called the Jews.
    * 


**the wall**  - This wall was very thick (2.5 meters) and was built to protect the city from attackers.
    * 


**ruled by other people**  - That is, another nation controlled them. The Jews were ruled by the Persians at this time, and later by other nations.
    * 


**once again**  - In some languages this might need to be translated as, “now” or, “as their ancestors had done” or, “just as before the Exile.”
    * 


**worshiped at the Temple**  - They worshiped Yahweh, the One True God, at the Temple they rebuilt.
    * 


//A Bible story from//  - These references may be slightly different in some Bible translations.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-12|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/20-the-exile-and-return|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-01|>>]]**


===== Messiah Will Defeat Satan [21-01] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-21-01.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=a6bc2e?nolink&640x360}}


**From the very beginning**, **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** planned to send the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/messiah|Messiah]]**. The first **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/promise|promise]]** of the Messiah came to **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/adam|Adam]]** and **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/eve|Eve]]**. God promised that a **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/descendant|descendant]]** of Eve would be born who would **crush the snake’s head**. **The snake who deceived Eve was [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/satan|Satan]]**. The promise meant that the Messiah would defeat Satan completely.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**From the very beginning**  - That is, from when the earth was first created.
    * 


**crush the snake’s head**  - Unless the head of a venomous snake is crushed, the snake can still hurt someone. Use a word for “crush” that communicates that its head is destroyed.
    * 


**The snake…was Satan**  – Satan spoke to Eve in the form of a snake. This does not mean that he is a snake now. This could be translated as, “The snake…was an appearance of Satan.”
    * 


**who deceived Eve**  - That is, “who lied to Eve.” The snake lied by making Eve doubt what God had said and tricking her into disobeying God.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__20-13|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/21-god-promises-the-messiah|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-02|>>]]**


===== A Promise for the Whole World [21-02] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-21-02.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=5491fa?nolink&640x360}}


**[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** promised **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/abraham|Abraham]]** that **through him**  all **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/people-group|people groups]]** of the world would receive a **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/bless|blessing]]**. This blessing would be **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/fulfill|fulfilled]]** when the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/messiah|Messiah]]** would come sometime in the future. He would make it possible for people from every people groups in the world to be **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/save|saved]]**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**through him**  – That is, “because of one of his descendants.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-01|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/21-god-promises-the-messiah|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-03|>>]]**


===== A Prophet Like Moses [21-03] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-21-03.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=91c111?nolink&640x360}}


**[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/promise|promised]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/moses|Moses]]** that in the future he would **raise up another [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophet]] like Moses**. This was another promise about the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/messiah|Messiah]]** who would come at some later time.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**raise up another prophet like Moses**  - That is, “appoint another prophet like Moses” or, “cause another prophet to come who would be like Moses.”
    * 


**prophet like Moses**  - To be like Moses, the future prophet would need to have great authority from God to lead and rescue his people.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-02|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/21-god-promises-the-messiah|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-04|>>]]**


===== A Descendant of David [21-04] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-21-04.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=dc6dbf?nolink&640x360}}


**[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/promise|promised]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/david|King David]]** that the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/messiah|Messiah]]** would be one of **David’s own [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/descendant|descendants]]**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**David's own descendants**  - Another way to say this would be, “a direct descendant of David himself.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-03|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/21-god-promises-the-messiah|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-05|>>]]**


===== The New Covenant [21-05] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-21-05.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=62aed8?nolink&640x360}}


**Through the [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophet]] [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/jeremiah|Jeremiah]]**, **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/promise|promised]]** that he would make a **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/covenant-new|New Covenant]]**, **but not like**  the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/covenant|covenant]]** God made with **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/israel|Israel]]** at **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/sinai|Sinai]]**. In the New Covenant, God would **write his law on the people’s hearts**, the people would **know God**  personally, they would **be his people**, and God would **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/forgive|forgive]]** their **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/sin|sins]]**. The **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/messiah|Messiah]]** would **start the New Covenant**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**Through the prophet Jeremiah God promised**  – This could be translated as, “Through the messages that God gave to Jeremiah, God promised” or, “The prophet Jeremiah told the people God's promise.”
    * 


**but not like**  - The New Covenant would be truly effective. People really would know God, they would truly live as his people, and He would forgive their sins completely, based on the Messiah's sacrifice of himself one time for all who believe in him.
    * 


**write his law on the people’s hearts**  - This is a metaphor meaning, “help his people to understand his laws and to earnestly desire to obey them.” If possible, keep the image of writing on their hearts, since this is in contrast with the way God had written his law on stone tablets for the Israelites. If that is not possible, you could just translate the meaning.
    * 


**be his people**  - This could be translated as, “be his special people” or, “be his favored people.”
    * 


**start the New Covenant**  - That is, “be the one to cause the New Covenant to take effect” or, “bring the New Covenant to his people.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-04|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/21-god-promises-the-messiah|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-06|>>]]**


===== Prophet, Priest and King [21-06] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-21-06.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=980b7e?nolink&640x360}}


**[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God's]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophets]]** also said that the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/messiah|Messiah]]** would be a prophet, a **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/priest|priest]]**, and a **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/king|king]]**. A prophet is a person who hears the words of God and then proclaims God’s words to the people. The Messiah that God promised to send would be the **perfect prophet**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**perfect prophet**  - The Messiah would be a prophet who is perfect in obedience to God, giving every word God would speak to the people. He would present God perfectly to the people, helping them to know and understand God.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-05|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/21-god-promises-the-messiah|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-07|>>]]**


===== The Perfect High Priest [21-07] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-21-07.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=b40cf7?nolink&640x360}}


**[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/israel|Israelite]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/priest|priests]]** made **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/sacrifice|sacrifices]]** to **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]] on behalf of**the people **as a substitute for the [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/punish|punishment]] for their [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/sin|sins]]**. Priests also **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/pray|prayed]]** to God for the people. The **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/messiah|Messiah]]** would be the **perfect [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/priest-high|high priest]]** who would **offer himself**  as a **perfect sacrifice**  to God.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**on behalf of**  - This may be translated as, “for the benefit of” or, “in the place of.”
    * 


**as a substitute for the punishment for their sins**  - God allowed people to bring animals to sacrifice for their sin as a reminder of the punishment that they deserved and their dependence on God to remove their sin. God accepted these sacrifices as a temporary covering for sin and did not punish the people for it.
    * 


**perfect high priest**  - Unlike the other high priests, the Messiah would never sin, and he would permanently take away all the sins of the people.
    * 


**offer himself**  – That is, “allow himself to be killed.”
    * 


**perfect sacrifice**  - That is, “a sacrifice that has no fault or imperfection.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-06|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/21-god-promises-the-messiah|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-08|>>]]**


===== Messiah Will Rule Forever [21-08] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-21-08.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=7af83e?nolink&640x360}}


A **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/king|king]]** is someone who rules over a **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/kingdom|kingdom]]** and **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/judge|judges]]** the people. The **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/messiah|Messiah]]** would be the perfect king who would **sit on the throne**  of his ancestor **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/david|David]]**. He would reign over **the whole world**  forever, and would always judge honestly and make the right decisions.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**sit on the throne of his ancestor David**  - A throne is a ceremonial chair for a king or queen that represents their authority. This expression could also be translated as, “have the authority to reign as his ancestor King David did” or, “be the descendant of King David and continue his rule over God's people.”
    * 


**the whole world**  - This could also be translated as, “everyone everywhere.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-07|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/21-god-promises-the-messiah|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-09|>>]]**


===== The Virgin Birth [21-09] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-21-09.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=c13a8c?nolink&640x360}}


**[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God's]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophets]]** predicted many other things about the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/messiah|Messiah]]**. The prophet **Malachi**  **foretold**  that a great prophet would come before the Messiah came. The prophet **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/isaiah|Isaiah]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophesied]]** that **the Messiah would be born from a [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/virgin|virgin]]**. The prophet **Micah**  said that he would be born in the town of **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/bethlehem|Bethlehem]]**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**Malachi**  - Malachi was the last prophet in the Old Testament.
    * 


**foretold**  - This could be translated as, “predicted” or, “prophesied.” It means to tell something that will happen in the future. Malachi spoke God's message to the people 400 years before the Messiah came.
    * 


**prophesied**  – In this context, “prophesied” has the same meaning as “foretold” and “predicted” since it means the prophet told something that would happen far in the future.
    * 


**the Messiah would be born from a virgin**  - Another way to say this would be, “a virgin would give birth to the Messiah.”
    * 


**Micah**  - Micah was an Old Testament prophet of God who, like Isaiah, spoke his messages from God almost 800 years before the Messiah came.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-08|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/21-god-promises-the-messiah|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-10|>>]]**


===== Messiah Will Heal [21-10] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-21-10.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=f91fd1?nolink&640x360}}


The **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophet]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/isaiah|Isaiah]]** said the Messiah would live in **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/galilee|Galilee]]**, comfort **broken-hearted people**, and **proclaim freedom to captives**  and **release to prisoners**. He also predicted that the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/messiah|Messiah]]** would **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/heal|heal]]** sick people and those who **could not hear, see, speak, or walk**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**broken-hearted people**  - This expression refers to people who are experiencing extreme sadness.
    * 


**proclaim freedom to captives**  - That is, “tell slaves they could be free.” This could also refer to freeing people from slavery to sin.
    * 


**release to prisoners**  - That is, “he will set free those who have unjustly been put into prison.” This could also refer to setting people free from the bondage of sin.
    * 


**could not hear, see, speak, or walk**  – It may be better to say, “could not hear, could not see, could not speak, or could not walk.” Some languages have special words for these conditions, such as “deaf” and “blind.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-09|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/21-god-promises-the-messiah|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-11|>>]]**


===== Messiah Will Be Betrayed [21-11] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-21-11.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=cda244?nolink&640x360}}


The **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophet]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/isaiah|Isaiah]]** also **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophesied]]** that the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/messiah|Messiah]]** would be **hated without reason and rejected**. Other prophets **foretold**  that those who killed the Messiah would **gamble for his clothes**  and that a friend would **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/betray|betray]]** him. The prophet **Zechariah**  predicted that the friend would be paid **thirty silver coins**  as payment for betraying the Messiah.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**hated without reason and rejected**  - This could be translated as, “hated and rejected, even though he had done nothing wrong” or “…even though he was innocent.”
    * 


**foretold**  – This means they told about things that would happen in the future. Other words that have a similar meaning are, “predicted” and “prophesied.”
    * 


**gamble for his clothes**  - That is, “play a game of chance to determine who would win his clothes.”
    * 


**Zechariah**  - Zechariah was an Old Testament prophet who spoke to God's people after they returned to the Promised Land from the Exile in Babylon. This was about 500 years before the Messiah came.
    * 


**thirty silver coins**  - At the time, each of these coins was worth the amount of money a person could earn in four days.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-10|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/21-god-promises-the-messiah|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-12|>>]]**


===== The Death of the Messiah [21-12] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-21-12.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=4c3805?nolink&640x360}}


The **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophets]]** also told about how the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/messiah|Messiah]]** would **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/death|die]]**. **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/isaiah|Isaiah]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophesied]]** that people would spit on, mock, and beat the Messiah. They would **pierce**  him and he would die in great suffering and agony, even though he had not done anything wrong.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**pierce**  - That is, “stab.” Sharp objects would penetrate his body as part of the punishment for people's sin.
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-11|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/21-god-promises-the-messiah|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-13|>>]]**


===== The Messiah Will Bring Peace [21-13] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-21-13.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=045f9f?nolink&640x360}}


The **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophets]]** also said that the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/messiah|Messiah]]** would be perfect, **having no [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/sin|sin]]**. He would **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/death|die]]** to **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/receive|receive]] the [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/punish|punishment]] for other people’s sin**. His punishment would bring **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/peace|peace]]** between **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** and people. For this reason, **it was God's will to crush the Messiah**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**having no sin**  - This can also be translated as “he never sinned.”
    * 


**receive the punishment for other people’s sin**  - That is, “to take on himself the punishment that other people deserved” or, “to be punished in the place of other people.”
    * 


**it was God's will**  - That is, “it fulfilled God's purpose.” This phrase means that the Messiah's death was exactly what God had planned to happen in order that his sacrifice would pay for the sins of the people.
    * 


**to crush**  - That is, “to damage completely,” “to kill” or, “to completely destroy.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-12|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/21-god-promises-the-messiah|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-14|>>]]**


===== Resurrection of the Messiah [21-14] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-21-14.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=d0517b?nolink&640x360}}


The **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophets]]** foretold that the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/messiah|Messiah]]** would **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/death|die]]** and that **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** would also **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/raise|raise]] him from the dead**. **Through the Messiah’s death and [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/resurrection|resurrection]], God would**accomplish his plan to **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/save|save]]** **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/sin|sinners]]** and **start the [[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/covenant-new|New Covenant]]**.


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**raise him from the dead**  - That is, “cause him to be alive again.”
    * 


**Through the Messiah’s death and resurrection, God would**  - This could also be translated as, “God would use the Messiah's death and resurrection to” or “The Messiah's death and resurrection would be the way that God would.”
    * 


**start the New Covenant**  – That is, “put the New Covenant into effect.”
**[[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-13|<<]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/21-god-promises-the-messiah|Up]] | [[http://door43.org/en/obs-training/sandbox/larrysallee/obs-training-text-and-notes#plugin_include__en__obs-training__frames__21-15|>>]]**


===== At the Perfect Time [21-15] =====


{{http://door43.org/_media/en/obs/obs-21-15.jpg?w=640&h=360&tok=511e76?nolink&640x360}}


**[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/god|God]]** revealed to the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/prophet|prophets]]** many things about the **[[http://door43.org/en/key-terms/messiah|Messiah]]**, but the Messiah did not come during the time of any of those prophets. More than 400 years after the last of these prophecies was given, at exactly the right time, God would send the Messiah **into the world**.


//A Bible story from: Genesis 3:15; 12:1-3; Deuteronomy 18:15; 2 Samuel 7; Jeremiah 31; Isaiah 59:16; Daniel 7; Malachi 4:5; Isaiah 7:14; Micah 5:2; Isaiah 9:1-7; 35:3-5; 61; 53; Psalm 22:18; 35:19; 69:4; 41:9; Zechariah 11:12-13; Isaiah 50:6; Psalm 16:10-11//


==== Translation Notes: ====


    * 


**into the world**  - This could be translated as, “to the people of the world.” The Messiah would be sent not only to the Jews, but to all people.
    * 


//A Bible story from//  - These references may be slightly different in some Bible translations.
